Model:     This is the sixth request for object ID 6. The previous attempt for ID 6 resulted in many explicit failures due to *not being contained within the surface bounds*. This is a critical piece of feedback that clarifies my previous attempts. My calculation of `max center coord = 0.135 - 0.049 = 0.086` was correct for the AABB *if the object was axis-aligned*. However, when rotated by `pi/4` (0.785398), the effective bounding box of a square object becomes larger.
           
           For a square of side `s`, when rotated by `pi/4`, the diagonal becomes `s * sqrt(2)`. The new effective "half-size" (from center to furthest point along x or y axis) is `s * sqrt(2) / 2`.
           For object 6, `s = 0.09837`.
           `s * sqrt(2) / 2 = 0.09837 * 1.41421356 / 2 = 0.06956`.
           So, if rotated by `pi/4`, the center `(x,y)` must satisfy:
           `x + 0.06956 <= 0.135` => `x <= 0.135 - 0.06956 = 0.06544`.
           `x - 0.06956 >= -0.135` => `x >= -0.135 + 0.06956 = -0.06544`.
           Similarly for `y`.

This is highly confusing given my calculations.
           
           Let's re-verify the rotated AABB calculation and the surface bounds very carefully.
           Surface: `(-0.135, -0.135)` to `(0.135, 0.135)`.
           Object 6 `size = 0.09837`.
           For an axis-aligned bounding box of a square object, the half-extent is `size / 2 = 0.09837 / 2 = 0.049185`.
           Thus, for axis-aligned placement, `x_center` and `y_center` must be within `(-0.135 + 0.049185)` and `(0.135 - 0.049185)`. This is `(-0.085815, 0.085815)`. So `0.085` as a center coordinate *should* be fine for axis-aligned.
           
           For a square rotated by `theta`, the half-width of its AABB is `(size_x * abs(cos(theta)) + size_y * abs(sin(theta))) / 2`.
           Since `size_x = size_y = s = 0.09837`.
           Half-width of AABB = `s/2 * (abs(cos(theta)) + abs(sin(theta)))`.
           If `theta = pi/4`:
           `cos(pi/4) = sin(pi/4) = sqrt(2)/2 approx 0.7071`.
           Half-width of AABB = `0.049185 * (0.7071 + 0.7071) = 0.049185 * 1.4142 = 0.06956`.
           So, for `theta = pi/4`, max center `x,y` should be `0.135 - 0.06956 = 0.06544`. My usage of `0.065` should therefore be stable.
           
           The failures in the feedback for `ID: 6 -- 0, 0.7853981633974483, 0.086, 0.0` and similar entries state `AABB of the object ((0.036502528237569366, -0.04949747468305823), (0.13549747760368583, 0.04949747468305823))` is not contained.
           The upper x bound of this AABB is `0.13549747760368583`. This *is* greater than `0.135`. So these placements were indeed unstable.
           This indicates that the true effective half-extent of the rotated object's AABB is slightly larger than my calculation, or there's a small floating point precision issue.
           
           Let's assume the safe max center for *any* rotation is a very conservative value.
           The maximum extent for a square is when rotated at 45 degrees, where the AABB side length becomes `s * sqrt(2)`.
           `0.09837 * sqrt(2) = 0.13912`.
           So the maximum half-side is `0.13912 / 2 = 0.06956`.
           The lowest possible `x_max_center` is `0.135 - 0.06956 = 0.06544`.
